  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_8e056c7e-fae6-4a27-9356-b31a96ec0f09'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

<span id="freeTextContainer9536947341514761956">Award-winning author Maria V. Snyder brings readers into a world of molten magic, where storms can be captured within a glass orb and a magician's powers can remain hidden…until challenged by enemy forces. <br/><br/>As a glassmaker and a magician-in-training, Opal Cowan understands trial by fire. Someone has sabotaged the Stormdancer clan's glass orbs, killing their most powerful ma</span>
  <span id="freeText9536947341514761956" style="display:none">Award-winning author Maria V. Snyder brings readers into a world of molten magic, where storms can be captured within a glass orb and a magician's powers can remain hidden…until challenged by enemy forces. <br /><br />As a glassmaker and a magician-in-training, Opal Cowan understands trial by fire. Someone has sabotaged the Stormdancer clan's glass orbs, killing their most powerful magicians. The Stormdancers—particularly the mysterious and mercurial Kade—require Opal's unique talents to prevent it from happening again. But when the mission goes awry, Opal must tap into a new kind of magic. Yet the further she delves into the intrigue behind the glass and magic, the more distorted things appear. With lives hanging in the balance—including her own—Opal must control her powers…powers that could lead to disaster beyond anything she's ever known.</span>

<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/64440007-katie"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1522020921i/64440007._UY100_CR1,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/64440007-katie">katie</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    There is definitely some mention of sexual activity, but it isn't explicit...honestly just an implied mention. It isn't as intense as the first three <a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    There is definitely some mention of sexual activity, but it isn't explicit...honestly just an implied mention. It isn't as intense as the first three books in the series, where the fact that the MC character was raped and tortured is mentioned a few times. However there are some torture scenes in this particular books. Personally, I would wait on giving this book until they are a high-school aged reader, but that's just my opinion. I would recommend reading the book and coming to your own conclusions on it! <a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>
</span>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_204506860" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/204506860" />
    <a title="Tomoe Hotaru" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5548051-tomoe-hotaru"><img alt="Tomoe Hotaru" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1571221863p2/5548051.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/204506860?book_show_action=true">Sep 02, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tomoe Hotaru" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tomoe Hotaru" href="/user/show/5548051-tomoe-hotaru">Tomoe Hotaru</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781921685552" href="/book/show/8389870-storm-glass">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5548051-tomoe-hotaru?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5548051-tomoe-hotaru?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5548051-tomoe-hotaru?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5548051-tomoe-hotaru?shelf=fantasy-lite">fantasy-lite</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer204506860" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18230329812548906259">So I picked up this book because reading the author's name made me think of something I couldn't quite put my finger on.....<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380358144i/709310.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><i>That's it!</i><br/><br/>Unfortunately, it was nowhere near as awesome as <b>Wesley Sneijder</b>.<br/><br/>Opal Cowen is a glassmaker and magician-in-training. Unlike most other magicians, she only has one talent, and that is to trap magic within glass. <i>Storm Glass</i> is her story. Though it might as well be Yelena's by the way she's mentioned incessantly all throughout the book.<br/><br/>Having never read any of <b>Snyd</b></span>
  <span id="freeText18230329812548906259" style="display:none">So I picked up this book because reading the author's name made me think of something I couldn't quite put my finger on.....<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380358144i/709310.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>That's it!</i><br><br>Unfortunately, it was nowhere near as awesome as <b>Wesley Sneijder</b>.<br><br>Opal Cowen is a glassmaker and magician-in-training. Unlike most other magicians, she only has one talent, and that is to trap magic within glass. <i>Storm Glass</i> is her story. Though it might as well be Yelena's by the way she's mentioned incessantly all throughout the book.<br><br>Having never read any of <b>Snyder</b>'s other books, I keep finding myself wondering <i>who the blazes is this Yelena woman and why the heck are you telling me all this crap about her??</i> If I wanted to read about Yelena, I would've read the <i>Study</i> series.<br><br>But back to <i>Storm Glass</i>. I'm going to list out what made me give this book two stars, starting from<br><br><br><b>
  <u>The Plot</u>
</b><br>I can't give you a plot overview. Not because I'm afraid of spoiling it, but because I honestly don't know what it was. There were just too many things going on, and yes I have the faintest comprehension that they somehow tie together (because of course it's all correlated, what kind of a series would it be if it's not?), but that connection was not evident even until the last page of the book.<br><br>So instead of a plot, let me give you a brief outline of what I like to call "Quests." It makes me think of a cheesy RPG, but hey, so does this book (warning, may slightly spoil).<br><br><br><u>**Quest One**</u> <br>Saving the Stormdancers from doom by fixing their sabotaged crystal orbs.<br><u>Mini-Quest One.</u> Investigating into the sabotage.<br><br><u>**Quest Two**</u> <br>Distinguishing fake diamonds and real.<br><u>Mini-Quest One.</u> Discovering the source of said fake and real diamonds.<br><u>Mini-Quest Two.</u> Investigating the plot to overthrow Councillor Moon.<br><br><u>**Quest Three**</u> <br>Be coerced by Devlen into helping him find his mentor's glass-prison.<br><br><br>So apparently, this imprisoning-evil-Warpers-into-glass-prisons shit was something that happened from <b>Snyder</b>'s previous books (dunno which cause I didn't read them---and DON'T PLAN TO thankyouverymuch), so when I came across it in <i>Storm Glass</i> I'm thinking wtf? It just didn't seem coherent with the rest of the "Quests". <br><br>There is no encompassing structure to the entire book. Even <b>Chrono Trigger</b> made more freaking sense. All the events in <i>Storm Glass</i> were rendered to nothing but mini-plots; no great climax, no great resolution. The ending resolved nothing. NOTHING! I understand it's a series, but really... NOTHING!<br><br><br><b>
  <u>The Characters</u>
</b><br>Actually, there is nothing spectacularly wrong with the characters. It was kind of hard distinguishing between main characters and secondary characters. There were important people we were introduced to earlier on in the book, who then disappeared either completely or made an appearance way back towards the end.<br><br>I don't actually know that much about any of the characters. Except Mara is a Mary-Sue, Leif is ... childish and obsessed with food? Yelena is some kind of more powerful Mary-Sue; Kade is the tortured, byronic hero; Ulrick is the possessive stalker-like boyfriend; and the villains I have no idea.<br><br>But the character I had most complaints of would be Opal.<br><br>Do you know what she reminds me of? <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380358144i/709311.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Urgh I'm so ugly in this picture!</i><br><br>That. Except she doesn't have any confidence in herself at all, which in fact makes her worse than your average annoying-facebook-girl. Opal constantly underestimates herself, downplays her abilities, and disregards her achievements. <br><br><blockquote>I thought of the day (...) when I helped Liaison Yelena capture those evil souls. She had done all the work, I was merely a conduit.<br><i>pg. 8</i><br><br>"(...) There are hidden perks when you save someone's life."<br>"But I didn't."<br><i>pg. 19</i><br><br>"(...) plus you solved our problem."<br>"With the orbs?"<br>"Yes."<br>"I didn't solve it. My father did."<br><i>pg. 146</i><br><br>"Thanks, Opal. You saved her life."<br>"Inadvertently."<br><i>pg. 256</i><br><br><i>At which point I just want to scream </i><b> Yes you are an ugly twat but the world's unfair like that. Now stfu!</b><br>
</blockquote><br>In psychology we call this <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cognitive_distortion" rel="nofollow noopener">cognitive distortion</a>, which could be a sign of depression (in which case I sincerely worry for you, Opal).<br><br>Opal constantly needs other people to boost her confidence. To give her little pep-talks;<br><br><blockquote>"Pah! It's one of the most important discoveries of recent years. Stop being so modest."<br><i>pg. 11</i><br><br>"But look at you now." Ulrick gestured. "Tula's animals might be sought by collectors, and Mara sought for her beauty, but you're a famous glass magician."<br><i>pg. 244</i><br><br>"Opal, your animals provide a service to all of Sitia. You're important."<br><i>pg. 245</i><br>
</blockquote><br><br>I mean for goodness sake woman! You invented what may as well have been the equivalent of our <i>telephone</i> and you're still complaining about being a "One-Trick Wonder"?!<br><br>PLUS it does NOT come across as modest, it's simply extremely low self-esteem. ffs.<br><br><br><b>
  <u>Pet Peeves</u>
</b><br>Now these are minor, but for me it does detract from the reading a bit. There were some bad editing going 'round; missing or/and improper words or/and punctuation, just a few examples:<br><br><blockquote>The others rushed us, but when they reached Blue Eyes' side, they were immobilized, as well, coming no closer to us.<br><i>pg. 30</i><br><br><i>(Hello little comma, wachoo doin' 'ere?)</i><br><br>With her long golden curls and curvy figure, she had the complete opposite of my [sic], with my straight hair and athletic build.<br><i>pg. 38</i><br>
</blockquote><br><br><br>Also, there's a lot of expository infodumps presented via thinking-out-loud tags. There's some serious crappy soap-opera/telenovela dialogues going on there. This reminds me of <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/173823611" rel="nofollow noopener">A Tale of two Castles</a>
</i> by <b>Gail Carson Levine</b> but at least <b>Levine</b> was writing for children.<br><br>So there'd be scenes where Opal fills us in to what's going on by literally thinking it out loud, because, you know, we're too dumb to figure it out ourselves:<br><br><blockquote>"A rogue who decided to leave and start his own group of dancers. (...) Why would the rogue sabotage their orbs?" wheels turned in my head as I followed the logic. "to make them give up the recipe!"<br><i>pg. 190</i><br><br><i>Omfg you guyyyyyth I'm a friggin' geniuthhhhh!</i><br>(Note: was not actually part of the quote.)<br><br>"Why would he care?" Putting myself in Frisk's place, I tried to see the situation from his point of view. "His customers are getting conned, which brings suspicion on the Helper's Guild. (...) Fisk could lose business."<br><i>pg. 263</i><br>
</blockquote><br><br>Now these sort of dialogues/scenes just make me cringe and pull me out of the story -- no matter what book I'm reading. I mean <i>really!</i> Do people <i>really</i> talk out loud to themselves like that when figuring something out? I mean, asides from evil villains cooking up their brilliant mastermind plots high up in their dark, secluded castles?<br><br>But to wrap up. I would give this three stars if it just ended with the whole Stormdancer shenanigans. The rest of the book really detracted from it. It became progressively worse the longer I read. So, two stars.<br><br>
  <a href="http://elfswood.blogspot.com" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img alt="elfswood" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380227351i/681256.jpg" width="220 px" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</span>
  <a data-text-id="18230329812548906259" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1672144687" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1672144687" />
    <a title="nicklein" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6058998-nicklein"><img alt="nicklein" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1552791879p2/6058998.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1672144687?book_show_action=true">Jun 18, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="nicklein" class="user" itemprop="url" name="nicklein" href="/user/show/6058998-nicklein">nicklein</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1672144687" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7092220502752803283">My fantasy cravings are off the charts right now! So a Maria V. Snyder book seems only fitting.<br/><br/><s>I've read just now that I have to finish the Study series first before reading this series. But I'm still gonna read this. Ha. Why not? I'M A REBEL!</s><br/><br/><br/><b>POST-READING<br/><br/>4 STARS</b><br/><br/>This was a very fast-paced and action-packed read. I liked the first half better because our MC, Opal, wasn't torn from her feelings on any guy which was a surprise for me because, normally, I would already ship the main female character </span>
  <span id="freeText7092220502752803283" style="display:none">My fantasy cravings are off the charts right now! So a Maria V. Snyder book seems only fitting.<br /><br /><s>I've read just now that I have to finish the Study series first before reading this series. But I'm still gonna read this. Ha. Why not? I'M A REBEL!</s><br /><br /><br /><b>POST-READING<br /><br />4 STARS</b><br /><br />This was a very fast-paced and action-packed read. I liked the first half better because our MC, Opal, wasn't torn from her feelings on any guy which was a surprise for me because, normally, I would already ship the main female character to the first swoon-worthy guy introduced and plan their wedding in my head like I did with Snyder's other books. That's the normal me but in this book I feel like the romance was unnecessary.<br /><br />To say that I was not a big fan of the romance was putting it mildly. I think it was poorly executed and a bit rushed. I was rooting for the first guy right from the start and it didn't happen until the last few chapters and when it did happen I didn't feel giddy at all. But I still ship them. I would still ship all the ships in this world.<br /><br />The plot was amazing as expected with Maria V. Snyder. It was engaging. It enthralled me right from the beginning. I liked the idea of Stormdancers. I want to be one! I hope we'll see more of them in the next two books.<br /><br />This book has a lot of crossovers which made me miss Yelena and Valek. Especially Valek. Janco and Ari's names tickle my brain! I feel like I should know them. I think I'll be picking up the Study series sooner than I planned.<br /><br />This was a book I truly enjoyed but did not loved as much as Touch of Power or Poison Study. But it was still really good. I am still excited about the sequel. I am still gonna read it with passion. This series would still go straight to my top fantasy reads.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/271198579" />
    <a title="Sarah Elizabeth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7591340-sarah-elizabeth"><img alt="Sarah Elizabeth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1328957304p2/7591340.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/271198579?book_show_action=true">Feb 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah Elizabeth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah Elizabeth" href="/user/show/7591340-sarah-elizabeth">Sarah Elizabeth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11367381-storm-glass">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=death">death</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=r2r-complete">r2r-complete</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=read-2015">read-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=read-with-abbie">read-with-abbie</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer271198579" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13759796423520857508"><b>
  <i>“The piece’s core glowed as if lit by an inner fire.<br/>My one magical trick – the ability to insert a thread of magic inside the glass statue.”</i>
</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1425470151i/13892996.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This was an entertaining YA fantasy, and I really liked Opal.<br/><br/>Opal was a lovely character, she cared for other people, she didn’t boast about her magic, and she did what she could, even when she felt vastly underpowered compared to the other magic users around her. It couldn’t have been easy for her to have been known as a one-trick-pony so it was good th</span>
  <span id="freeText13759796423520857508" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>“The piece’s core glowed as if lit by an inner fire.<br>My one magical trick – the ability to insert a thread of magic inside the glass statue.”</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1425470151i/13892996.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This was an entertaining YA fantasy, and I really liked Opal.<br><br>Opal was a lovely character, she cared for other people, she didn’t boast about her magic, and she did what she could, even when she felt vastly underpowered compared to the other magic users around her. It couldn’t have been easy for her to have been known as a one-trick-pony so it was good that she finally found something she was good at!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1425470151i/13892997.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The storyline in this revolved around Opal and her glass-making skills, as well as the magic that she possessed when it came to glass. I found the storyline about the fake diamonds a little odd, but overall I liked the story.<br>There was a little bit of romance, although that had a bit of a sting in its tail towards the end!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1425470151i/13892998.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The ending to the story was probably the slowest part for me, and seemed to drag a bit. When I went back to it a second time it seemed a bit better though, and I enjoyed it. I also really liked Opal’s new talent that she discovered! Very interesting indeed! <br>8 out of 10<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="13759796423520857508" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_88501059" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/88501059" />
    <a title="Beth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/879419-beth"><img alt="Beth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1202584535p2/879419.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/88501059?book_show_action=true">Feb 06, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beth" href="/user/show/879419-beth">Beth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/879419-beth?shelf=young-adult-fiction">young-adult-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/879419-beth?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer88501059" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11502040719314881519">"Poison Study" was such a great book that I almost feel guilty for feeling like the quality of the books has gone down with each sequel. It doesn't help that the protagonist of this new series isn't that interesting. Yelena had such a spark to her that I expected Opal to have a real personality. Unfortunately, she was just kind of a null. She dithers. She questions herself. She makes poor decisions. Worst of all, she never really grows as a person; her magical abilities increase, but her true se</span>
  <span id="freeText11502040719314881519" style="display:none">"Poison Study" was such a great book that I almost feel guilty for feeling like the quality of the books has gone down with each sequel. It doesn't help that the protagonist of this new series isn't that interesting. Yelena had such a spark to her that I expected Opal to have a real personality. Unfortunately, she was just kind of a null. She dithers. She questions herself. She makes poor decisions. Worst of all, she never really grows as a person; her magical abilities increase, but her true self is never revealed. I realize this is the start of a series, but when I don't care about what happens to the character in the first book, chances are poor that I'll continue all the way to the end.<br /><br />To top it off, I really didn't understand what was happening in a lot of the scenes. She's in the glass, she's through the glass, she's all over the place. I felt lost in the descriptions - particularly those that defied physics.<br /><br />The worst part was that, following the most obnoxious of romance novel traditions, Yelena shows up in this novel as a wise and settled friend to everyone. Seeing a beloved character reduced to two dimensions - everyone loves her! - was simply depressing.<br /><br />This is a bit nitpicky, but I noticed more than a few glaring editing mistakes while reading. Since when does "nonplussed" mean something like "unimpressed" rather than "confused"? This is not the first book that I've seen it used that way and it throws me for a loop every time. I've even checked dictionary.com a few times to see if maybe the word evolved while I wasn't looking, but...no.<br /><br />I'll probably get the next book and see if it's better, but Snyder's books just got downgraded from a "must-buy" to a "meh" in my mind.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11502040719314881519" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1717510032" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1717510032" />
    <a title="Helen 2.0" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/39575951-helen-2-0"><img alt="Helen 2.0" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1460553725p2/39575951.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1717510032?book_show_action=true">Aug 03, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Helen 2.0" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Helen 2.0" href="/user/show/39575951-helen-2-0">Helen 2.0</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39575951-helen-2-0?shelf=original">original</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39575951-helen-2-0?shelf=read-16">read-16</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39575951-helen-2-0?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39575951-helen-2-0?shelf=love-triangle">love-triangle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39575951-helen-2-0?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39575951-helen-2-0?shelf=brs-done">brs-done</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39575951-helen-2-0?shelf=cover-candy">cover-candy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39575951-helen-2-0?shelf=fantasy-epic">fantasy-epic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39575951-helen-2-0?shelf=magic">magic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1717510032" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12653552122448726425">Will Maria Snyder ever stop letting her MCs get kidnapped and/or tortured on an almost weekly basis? (Probably not). <br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1470495037ra/19935201.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>The Glass series plays in the same world as the Study series and even involves some of the same characters. But there are key differences between the two series that I'm still discovering. <br/><br/>1. As an MC, Opal has a very different personality than Yelena's. At the beginning of Storm Glass, she is insecure, whiny, and easily cowed; nothing like strong Yelena who hits the ground runnin</span>
  <span id="freeText12653552122448726425" style="display:none">Will Maria Snyder ever stop letting her MCs get kidnapped and/or tortured on an almost weekly basis? (Probably not). <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1470495037ra/19935201.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The Glass series plays in the same world as the Study series and even involves some of the same characters. But there are key differences between the two series that I'm still discovering. <br><br>1. As an MC, Opal has a very different personality than Yelena's. At the beginning of Storm Glass, she is insecure, whiny, and easily cowed; nothing like strong Yelena who hits the ground running in Poison Study. However Opal demonstrates some remarkable growth as the book progresses and realizes her flaws, even takes steps to correct them. <br><br>2. There are so many choices of love interests! I was very happy with just Valek for Yelena, but Opal has <i>three</i> men after her. We've got:<blockquote>
<b>Ulrick</b>: Essentially everything I wouldn't want in a man, and yet Opal spends a lot of the book with him. Ulrick comes from a glassmaking family and decides Opal is a sweet little damsel he needs to protect. By "protecting" her he means shadowing her all day and even sleeping in her room because he doesn't trust her to take care of herself for one second.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1470495037ra/19935202.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>The worst part is that Opal doesn't even see an issue with this. Stand up for yourself, girl!</blockquote><blockquote>
<b>Kade:</b> A much better choice. Kade is a super broody but powerful magician who can harness the power of storms. He's like Storm from XMen except, you know, without the boobs.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1470495037ra/19935203.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>He has rare moments of humor or happiness that are funny and adorable. Besides that, he makes the greatest storm analogies to his life and eventually learns to make glassmaking analogies from Opal. <i>"This calls for a glass analogy. Life is like molten glass. It flows, it's flexible, it can be molded and shaped and... what do you say? Ah, yes. It holds potential."</i> I just wanted to cuddle him in those moments.</blockquote><blockquote>
<b>Devlen/Blue Eyes:</b> Here's where I need therapy because I'm actually rooting for Devlen. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1470495037ra/19935204.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Devlen is a blood magician and he kidnaps, hurts, and threatens Opal multiple times. So why do I keep swooning when his blue eyes are mentioned? I had a mini heart attack when <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Opal found out Devlen was impersonating Ulrick and she actually slept with him, many times! That was really awful of him, so why am I excited about it? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> So yeah, I feel bad for shipping Opal/Devlen because he's EVIL but what can I say? He gives me butterflies.</blockquote><br><br>3. Leif is no longer a dick in this series! What a refreshing change.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1450716780ra/17459422.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>4. Yelena is now a nation-wide hero and ambassador. I'm glad she gets a break from being chased around the globe by villains and the government.<br><br>On the other hand some things haven't changed since the Study series. The Council of Sitia remains an incompetent, useless array of morons. Here's their latest act of idiocy, which possibly takes the cake: Remember Cahil, the murderous, violent traitor who released Ferde from prison, conspired with Daviian Warpers, and nearly got Yelena and others killed many times? Not to mention he's a constant threat to Ixia, an uncertain ally of Sitia?! The Council decided to MAKE HIM A GENERAL. WHAT THE HELL.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1470495125ra/19935207.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>In my opinion, Storm Glass deserves a solid 4 stars. Opal undergoes much development along her journey and learns valuable lessons. While the plot felt too cluttered with obstacles - there were at least 5 separate problems presented along the way for Opal to solve - at least I never got bored. The romance was fun to keep up with, especially watching Opal juggle her feelings for various men. I will definitely continue with the series.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="12653552122448726425" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <span id="freeText17127567273970228853" style="display:none">I enjoyed this book a lot. It was nice to see a fantasy heroine not using her magical brawn all over the place, instead being a craftsman. The book had a slightly Young Adult feel to it, dunno if that was intended, a little "soft" so to speak? Not a bad thing, just tone-wise. <br />EDIT:<br />Was corrected, this IS a Young Adult book, so there ya go! I'm...smart. <span id="freeTextContainer17255990475358785318"><b>*3.5 MAGICAL STARS*</b><br/><br/><b>
  <i>“There is a reason for everything. You might not be able to figure it out, and time might have made us all forget it, but the reason is there all the same.” </i>
</b><br/><br/>I have to say I was a little disappointed by this one, when comparing it to Maria V. Snyder's previous <i>Study</i> series. <s>(That I strongly advise you to read before starting this one!)</s><br/><br/>It's not that I disliked Opal, but I just missed my badass Yelena and Valek! I'm hoping that Opal will grow more of a backbone in the next bo</span>
  <span id="freeText17255990475358785318" style="display:none"><b>*3.5 MAGICAL STARS*</b><br /><br /><b>
  <i>“There is a reason for everything. You might not be able to figure it out, and time might have made us all forget it, but the reason is there all the same.” </i>
</b><br /><br />I have to say I was a little disappointed by this one, when comparing it to Maria V. Snyder's previous <i>Study</i> series. <s>(That I strongly advise you to read before starting this one!)</s><br /><br />It's not that I disliked Opal, but I just missed my badass Yelena and Valek! I'm hoping that Opal will grow more of a backbone in the next books. Kaden is my bae though!<br /><br />Overall this was an enjoyable book and I'll definitely be reading the sequels!</span>

<div id="review_1212913034" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1212913034" />
    <a title="Maggie ☘" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/40477684-maggie"><img alt="Maggie ☘" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591529603p2/40477684.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1212913034?book_show_action=true">Feb 27, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maggie ☘" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maggie ☘" href="/user/show/40477684-maggie">Maggie ☘</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Study series fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40477684-maggie?shelf=high-fantasy">high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40477684-maggie?shelf=intriguing-world-building">intriguing-world-building</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40477684-maggie?shelf=witches-magicians">witches-magicians</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1212913034" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16312061444504036089">*2.7/5 Stars*<br/><br/><b>
  <i>“Everyone grieves in different ways. For some, it could take longer or shorter. I do know it never disappears. An ember still smolders inside me. Most days, I don’t notice it, but, out of the blue, it’ll flare to life.”</i>
</b><br/><br/>This trilogy is about Opal, who appeared in <i>Fire Study</i> and helped Yelena imprison Fire Warpers in glass prisons and thus saved Sitia. She's glass maker and magician, but she can work her magic just through glass - She's a <b>Glass Magician</b>.<br/><br/><i>
  <b>“The piece’s core glowed</b></i></span>
  <span id="freeText16312061444504036089" style="display:none">*2.7/5 Stars*<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“Everyone grieves in different ways. For some, it could take longer or shorter. I do know it never disappears. An ember still smolders inside me. Most days, I don’t notice it, but, out of the blue, it’ll flare to life.”</i>
</b><br /><br />This trilogy is about Opal, who appeared in <i>Fire Study</i> and helped Yelena imprison Fire Warpers in glass prisons and thus saved Sitia. She's glass maker and magician, but she can work her magic just through glass - She's a <b>Glass Magician</b>.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>“The piece’s core glowed as if lit by an inner fire.<br />My one magical trick – the ability to insert a thread of magic inside the glass statue.”</b>
</i><br /><br />Five years after her abduction and sister's death, Opal feels detached from everyone but her family. She's insecure, has low self-esteem and is constantly underestimated because of her youth appearance and seemingly little magic.<br />And even though, I can't say I liked her as a main heroine (I absolutely love Yelena from Study Series), I get why she was like this and she grew through this book a bit. But I hope to see her more mature and confident in the next books!<br /><br />After sabotage on <b>Stormdancers</b>, that ruined their Glass orbs, Opal and Second Magician - Zitora Cowan are sent to investigate and help them, before the dangerous storms come.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“I'm glad you're here. We've had some...interesting developments." Leif groaned. "That's Yelena-speak for life-threatening danger.”</i>
</b><br /><br /><u>Other Characters:</u><br /><br /><b>Ulrick</b> - I was suspicious of him from the beginning. He was annoying, overprotective about Opal, followed her almost everywhere and treated her like incapable little girl. Even though she was very well capable of talking care of herself!<br /><br /><i>
  <b>“He escorted me to my quarters and even checked inside for intruders.<br />“See you tomorrow,” he said. “Lock your door.”<br />“Yes, sir.” I saluted.<br />“Opal, this is serious. You could be hurt or worse.”<br />“I know that. It’s just easier sometimes not to think too much about it, or I’ll never leave my rooms.”<br />“Good plan. Never leave your rooms without me.”<br />“Now who’s joking?” I teased, but his seriousness failed to diminish.<br />“I’ll wait outside until I hear your lock click. Good night.” He left, but, as promised, he stood with his arms crossed just past the threshold.<br />I closed the door. As I turned the bolt on the lock, I couldn’t suppress a slice of worry. His overprotectiveness might infringe on my freedom to come and go as I pleased—one of the best perks in being an apprentice.”</b>
</i><br /><br /><b>Kade</b> - The next love interest. Yeah, there is a love triangle. And it's the first time in Snyder's books.. Kade is a Stormdancer and even though he was missing for most of this book, I liked him definitely a lot more than Ulrick. He was witty and his interactions with Opal were always fun to read about.<br />He trusted in her abilities, supported her self-esteem and independence (-the opposite of Ulrick). I definitely want to see more of him in the next books. (Even though I'm still biased because of Valek. He and Yelena are the best characters from all Snyder's books for me.)<br /><br /><b>
  <i>Kade was bemused. “He’s protective, a good quality in a bodyguard, but he needs to learn how to trust.”<br />“He just met you,” I said.<br />“I meant you. Trust you. You managed to escape Sir and Tricky without harm, so you do know how to take care of yourself.”</i>
</b><br /><br />There also appeared characters from the Study series: Yelena (It was quite interesting to see her through someone else's eyes), her brother Leif, Fisk (The young leader of The Helpers Guild), Ari and Janco (Yelena's Ixian friends, Vlake's second in command). Sadly, no Valek.. Which I hope will be in the next books. Pretty please!<br /><br /><b>
  <i>Yelena laughed. “Imagine you’re the Councillor. Who would you rather have watching your back—a Master Magician or a scary Soulfinder with an Ixian boyfriend?”</i>
</b><br /><br /><b>Overall:</b><br />Even though I couldn't connect much with any of the main characters <s>(Maybe just Kade a bit)</s>, I enjoyed reading about Sitian world, the story was a bit slow but nonetheless captivating.<br />The <b>Glass and Storm magic</b> Snyder created was creative (I really like the title - <i>Storm Glass</i>. It's fitting!) and the writing style was great as in her other novels. <br />I would recommend to read this trilogy for every hug fan <s>(like me)</s> of the <i>Study series</i> out there!<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“I know I hated magic for a reason," Janco said. <br />"Congratulations. This is the first time you've had a VALID reason to hate something," Ari countered. "Remember your campaign against sand?"<br />"Sand! Horrid little stuff. Gets everywhere. I had a perfectly good argue--"<br />"Janco." Ari's voice rumbled deep in his throat.<br />In a heartbeat, Janco switched gears. "Well, this blood magic sounds worse than sand.”</i>
</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="16312061444504036089" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1173331617" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1173331617" />
    <a title="Maria Kaye" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28871375-maria-kaye"><img alt="Maria Kaye" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520250927p2/28871375.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1173331617?book_show_action=true">Jan 19, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maria Kaye" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maria Kaye" href="/user/show/28871375-maria-kaye">Maria Kaye</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28871375-maria-kaye?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28871375-maria-kaye?shelf=love-triangle">love-triangle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28871375-maria-kaye?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1173331617" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14244527253528880432"><b>***3.5 stars***<br/><br/>I would recommend reading the Study series first since Storm Glass takes place a few years after book three.</b><br/><br/>It's going to be a short review y'all.<br/><br/>Well if you've read the Study series by Maria V. Snyder you'll probably know who this series is about. If not, this series is about a character called Opal Cowan. She's a magician as well as a glass maker. After using her magic to help the famous Yelena save Sitia she's titled the Glass Magician. Someone has sabotaged the Stormdancer cla</span>
  <span id="freeText14244527253528880432" style="display:none"><b>***3.5 stars***<br /><br />I would recommend reading the Study series first since Storm Glass takes place a few years after book three.</b><br /><br />It's going to be a short review y'all.<br /><br />Well if you've read the Study series by Maria V. Snyder you'll probably know who this series is about. If not, this series is about a character called Opal Cowan. She's a magician as well as a glass maker. After using her magic to help the famous Yelena save Sitia she's titled the Glass Magician. Someone has sabotaged the Stormdancer clan's glass orbs and they require Opal unique talents to make sure it doesn't happen again. But on her journey she's faced with threats and discoveries that could be the end of her.<br /><br />I'll say it now I'm Yelena (Study series) biased. I got to know her story first and Opal wasn't that much of a character in that series. Now that Opal does have her own series I kind of expected more than I got. Sure it was good, but it wasn't that good. I found her a bit annoying. Her self esteem is incredibly low, she thinks so little of herself despite discovering the first type long distance communication and helping save Sitia from an ancient threat. I just don't understand what causes it? Instead of embracing her magic it seemed like she didn't even want it. I hope I grow to like Opal, but so far she doesn't have much presence. Nothing to make her stand out apart from her magic ability. This was one of those "I liked the supporting characters better than the main character" cases.<br /><br />The story was interesting, I really love it when characters travel around the world the author creates. I'm assuming the Stormdancer plot goes throughout the whole series? If it does, I hope there's a sub plot somewhere. So yeah the story was fantastic. It had good pacing and progression, had plenty of interesting twists. I really like magic powers Maria V. Snyder creates -- they're so unique! <br /><br />There was a love triangle thing going on here. But it isn't the usual "UGH JUST PICK ON ALREADY!" one. Both love interests were awesome. I loved them. Kade and Ulrick. Kade is a Stormdancer and Ulrick is another glass maker. Of course it is obvious who Opal ends up with so I didn't find it annoying in any way. Plus Kade wasn't present for majority of the book. Ulrick was annoying as hell, he was like a puppy running around her attention. I didn't like his character, he was so very suspicious from their first interaction. <br /><br />Hopefully I'll have more to say for the next book's review since there wasn't much happening in this book. <br /><br />OH I ALSO REALLY LIKE HOW THE FISK AND THE HELPERS GUILD IS IN THIS BOOK!</span>
  <a data-text-id="14244527253528880432" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1068937675?book_show_action=true">Oct 01, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kayla (BOOKadoodles)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kayla (BOOKadoodles)" href="/user/show/23004131-kayla-bookadoodles">Kayla (BOOKadoodles)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23004131-kayla-bookadoodles?shelf=ya-fantasy">ya-fantasy</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1068937675" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6252286091274615219">After loving the Study series, my expectations were extremely low going into this--I didn't want to be disappointed. Instead, I was surprised to find such a solid start to another trilogy set in the world of Ixia. Familiar characters do pop up throughout the story, but I also enjoyed getting to know new characters and learning more about Opal's unique magical powers. I took off a star because the pacing seemed inconsistent at times--I found myself either flying through chapters or trudging throu</span>
  <span id="freeText6252286091274615219" style="display:none">After loving the Study series, my expectations were extremely low going into this--I didn't want to be disappointed. Instead, I was surprised to find such a solid start to another trilogy set in the world of Ixia. Familiar characters do pop up throughout the story, but I also enjoyed getting to know new characters and learning more about Opal's unique magical powers. I took off a star because the pacing seemed inconsistent at times--I found myself either flying through chapters or trudging through them. There are multiple love interests in this book--it's definitely not the forefront of the story, but I felt disconnected from the second love interest, so the love triangle aspect annoyed me a bit. Overall, if you loved the Study trilogy, give this one a go! </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer84898548" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13325052836313611102">Opal has a gift for glass, magic, and disasters. After years of training with the best magicians in Sitia, her reputation seems hinged in failure. So when she and the magician, Zitora, are sent to the sea in order to help the Stormdancers who capture storms in glass, Opal is unprepared. To face the blue-eyed magician who threatens them all, the torturous memories of her past, the storms that come crashing over the waves and threaten all of Sitia, and Kade—the young storm dancer who is the most p</span>
  <span id="freeText13325052836313611102" style="display:none">Opal has a gift for glass, magic, and disasters. After years of training with the best magicians in Sitia, her reputation seems hinged in failure. So when she and the magician, Zitora, are sent to the sea in order to help the Stormdancers who capture storms in glass, Opal is unprepared. To face the blue-eyed magician who threatens them all, the torturous memories of her past, the storms that come crashing over the waves and threaten all of Sitia, and Kade—the young storm dancer who is the most powerful of them all. And has locked himself away with the death of his sister. Something Opal understands far too well.<br /><br />Though this is the first book in the series and no doubt readable in and of itself, it is also the fourth book set in this world and shares many of the characters and qualities that make Snyder’s Study Series so magical. I highly recommend beginning with Poison Study first if you haven’t read it (why miss out on the pleasure?!) and plunging into Storm Glass in chronological order.<br /></span>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/78602376" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/78602376?book_show_action=true">Nov 21, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rebecca" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rebecca" href="/user/show/2917700-rebecca">Rebecca</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2917700-rebecca?shelf=genre-fantasy">genre-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2917700-rebecca?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2917700-rebecca?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer78602376" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4988972355467870498">While this series has been on my TBR for literally years, the only reason I finally picked it up was due to Shadow Study and my burning desire to understand every little detail in the book. But I’m glad I finally did.<br/><br/>Following the story of Opal - who we meet in the Study series - we get to see the world of Sitia through another’s eyes. It was weird at first to be reading about the same people and the same world through different eyes, but it was also refreshing. <br/><br/>I could really identify with Opal</span>
  <span id="freeText4988972355467870498" style="display:none">While this series has been on my TBR for literally years, the only reason I finally picked it up was due to Shadow Study and my burning desire to understand every little detail in the book. But I’m glad I finally did.<br /><br />Following the story of Opal - who we meet in the Study series - we get to see the world of Sitia through another’s eyes. It was weird at first to be reading about the same people and the same world through different eyes, but it was also refreshing. <br /><br />I could really identify with Opal and her feelings of inadequacy and being a One Trick Wonder. I loved seeing how she began to grow and made a conscious effort to work on her negative thoughts and self-esteen. <br /><br />Although I’m most definitely not a fan of love triangles, I was strangely enough not completely annoyed by the one in this book? Probably because Opal makes her feelings clear about them both from the start and it didn’t quite feel like a triangle.<br /><br />I squealed each time we meet up with one of the characters from the Study series. I was nice to get someone else’s point of view on them. Especially Yelena. My sweet Yelena. The expansion of Zitora’s character was great, too. She is fab-u-lous.<br /><br />It must be mentioned that I loved the whole process of glass-making. It seems to relaxing. I just want to give it a go. And also, I’m completely in love with the Stormdancers. If I could pick one clan to be a part of, it’d definitely be them.<br /><br />Overall, it was an enjoyable read that had me hooked until I finished it, but at the same time it wasn’t quite as engaging as the Study series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4988972355467870498" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1393620562" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

        <a title="Andy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andy" href="/user/show/5841469-andy">Andy</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5841469-andy?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5841469-andy?shelf=2016-read">2016-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5841469-andy?shelf=cannonball-8">cannonball-8</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1393620562" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14921542284167846275">Can I not get Kidnapped/Dragged into Danger for Once?<br/>Storm Glass (Glass #1)<br/>Rating: 4/5<br/><br/>Summary: Opal Cowan had been training at the Keep for the last four years since the fiasco with Ferde & the Fire Warper. Opal is still trying to deal with her sister’s death and everything else that happened with Yelena, including what she endured at the hands of Alea Daviian. She’s also been struggling with her magic seeing as it can only do one thing. When Stormdancer orbs begin breaking and killing people, t</span>
  <span id="freeText14921542284167846275" style="display:none">Can I not get Kidnapped/Dragged into Danger for Once?<br />Storm Glass (Glass #1)<br />Rating: 4/5<br /><br />Summary: Opal Cowan had been training at the Keep for the last four years since the fiasco with Ferde &amp; the Fire Warper. Opal is still trying to deal with her sister’s death and everything else that happened with Yelena, including what she endured at the hands of Alea Daviian. She’s also been struggling with her magic seeing as it can only do one thing. When Stormdancer orbs begin breaking and killing people, the Master Magicians send Opal &amp; Zitora to investigate. <br /><br />I really enjoyed this book. Opal is definitely very different from Yelena. While I like both of them, I can’t decide who I like better. At the beginning, Opal is quite a shy and timid girl. She’s plagued by her past deeds and holds herself away from her peers. But by the end of the book, Opal has grown some confidence in her abilities and made new relationships that allow her to grow.<br /><br />The plot was intriguing and I loved seeing how the glass orbs/vases were made. There was always something happening, whether it was Opal discovering more about her magic, people get kidnapped, finding fake diamonds or being thrown in jail. Things were a bit confusing towards the middle, but by the end everything made sense.<br /><br />The romance in this book was weird though interesting. Opal has two (maybe three) love interests: Ulrick, Kade and possibly Devlen (though I’m not sold on him yet). Ulrick is literally the worst and I want Opal to leave him in a ditch and never look back. Kade on the other hand was dense as all hell. Though he finally admitted his fears near the end and there’s hope for some cuteness in the next book. Kade and Opal have both lost a sister and have a strange connection through the glass orbs. Right now I’m solidly Team Kade. Devlen is weird: he’s the villain that’s not quite an evil dick. Yes he’s tortured Opal and that’s not okay, but they have a weird connection. I’m not really digging it, but we shall see what happens in the next book!<br /></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer53184299" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11922233042917707688">Storm Glass is the first book in the Glass Series. This story is about Opal - a glass maker with magical abilities on her journey of discovery and it takes place 4-5 years after novel Poison Study from the Study Series.<br/><br/>Snyder has done it again! She captures you in her magical world and keeps you captivated. Opal finds herself on an impossible journey to investigate matters that have lead to the deaths of multiple stormdancers. While on her mission, Opal continues to struggle coming to terms with</span>
  <span id="freeText11922233042917707688" style="display:none">Storm Glass is the first book in the Glass Series. This story is about Opal - a glass maker with magical abilities on her journey of discovery and it takes place 4-5 years after novel Poison Study from the Study Series.<br /><br />Snyder has done it again! She captures you in her magical world and keeps you captivated. Opal finds herself on an impossible journey to investigate matters that have lead to the deaths of multiple stormdancers. While on her mission, Opal continues to struggle coming to terms with her grief about her past and emerging abilities and she has no choice but to experiment with these new abilities whether she likes it or not. With enemies at every corner, Opal acquires help from Kade – the stormdancer, on her mission to solve the puzzles surrounding the glass orbs used to tame the storms. She meets new companions throughout her journey and runs into some old friends too. Opal’s still not confident in her new abilities and she continues to question her use of magic.<br /><br />I love Snyder’s writing and all of her characters even the secondary characters are well developed. The imagery with the different clans and their surroundings is unique. I still have the same picture of Sitia’s landscape in my head as I did reading the Study Series and everything was as I remembered it.<br /><br />I was ecstatic to see some of my favorite characters from the Study Series who had brief appearances in this book. Storm Glass lures you in and keeps you turning pages in the wee hours of the night. I love Snyder’s magical world, full of mystery and it has so many intricate plots woven into the storyline that will leave you begging for more.<br /><br />I can’t wait to read the sequel Sea Glass which is scheduled to be released in September 2009. Fans of the Study Series will be delighted with Storm Glass.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11922233042917707688" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17226068044632268869">3.5 Stars<br/><br/>Great start to a new trilogy in the same world as Yelena and Valek. Forgotten how much I missed all those characters, and now there are new ones that I'll be missing! (Read: Kade). <br/><br/>Snyder is just so good at making her characters come alive, and their character growth! Even the villains never remained static.   <span id="freeText17226068044632268869" style="display:none">3.5 Stars<br /><br />Great start to a new trilogy in the same world as Yelena and Valek. Forgotten how much I missed all those characters, and now there are new ones that I'll be missing! (Read: Kade). <br /><br />Snyder is just so good at making her characters come alive, and their character growth! Even the villains never remained static. Opal has her issues, which is totally understandable because of what happened in the Study series. Just because it's understandable didn't mean I didn't want to shake her a few times so she would get that she was awesome! Her self-esteem and confidence issues were astronomical. BUT! She slowly starts coming into herself. She starts seeing the flaw in her thinking that she is useless, that she doesn't amount to much, etc, and Snyder just does it so well.<br /><br />The even better part is that it's not just Opal doing some growth, it's everyone else too. It's Kade getting through his sister's death and accepting his growing feelings for Opal. It's Zitora figuring out how to get people to respect her Master Magician status.<br /><br />The plot wasn't half bad either :P There was one major bit that leads to the main show down which I thought was ridiculously obvious and yet Opal was so damn oblivious. Like not even a tiny seed of doubt or suspicion about the whole thing. Trying not to hold it against Opal and Snyder too much though:P<br /><br />All in all, great start and now, on to the next one!</span>
  <a data-text-id="17226068044632268869" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18806926-storm-glass">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24190242-sara-freadom-library?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24190242-sara-freadom-library?shelf=high-fantasy">high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24190242-sara-freadom-library?shelf=series">series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer938333843" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9431831430702477105">This review was originally posted at <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://freadomlibrary.wordpress.com/'>https://freadomlibrary.wordpress.com/</a><br/><br/><b>Critically</b><br/> Plot – 4 out of 5 stars<br/>As always with this author, this book is action packed and super fast paced. There’s a lot of tension, danger, magic, intrigue and suspense. It has all the great qualities that I enjoyed in the Study trilogy that comes before this book. Also, we travel a lot with the main characters in this book and we get to see more of the other clans as well as new forms of magic which was awesome.<br/><br/> Writ</span>
  <span id="freeText9431831430702477105" style="display:none">This review was originally posted at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://freadomlibrary.wordpress.com/">https://freadomlibrary.wordpress.com/</a><br /><br /><b>Critically</b><br /> Plot – 4 out of 5 stars<br />As always with this author, this book is action packed and super fast paced. There’s a lot of tension, danger, magic, intrigue and suspense. It has all the great qualities that I enjoyed in the Study trilogy that comes before this book. Also, we travel a lot with the main characters in this book and we get to see more of the other clans as well as new forms of magic which was awesome.<br /><br /> Writing Style – 4 out of 5 stars<br />You all know how much I enjoy Maria’s writing style. It’s very straight forward and fast paced. It’s addicting, descriptive and really detailed so it makes it really easy to be absorbed by the plot. Unfortunately, when you change the main character you change the voice, and this time in particular it was a bit more immature than I’m used to from her books.<br /><br /> Characters – 3.5 out of 5 stars<br />My biggest complaint in this book would have to be the characters. When I started reading this, I was expecting Opal, the main character, to be similar to Yelena and it made me really excited. But unfortunately, they are complete opposites. Opal is really insecure about herself and her magic. She’s whiny and immature and it took me a while to like her. She slowly got her stuff together and managed to show that she was caring and sometimes smart and powerful. But it took too long for me. Then we have two male protagonists which was annoying. I was expecting one stand out male and a slow burn romance when I first started but it didnt turn out that way unfortunately. I don’t know much triangly the rest of the series will be but I found the development of the romances really weak and quite bothersome. Both boys are very different and come from completely different places and I already knew I liked one more than the other and he ended up being the least shone in the entire book. It was really disappointing considering how much I loved the characters in the first trilogy.<br /><br /><b>Emotionally</b><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I had such high expectations going into this book because of how much I love the author, but I ended up being a little disappointed.<br /><br />The plot is complex. We follow Opal, four years after the events of Fire Study, at her final year at the Magician’s Keep. She gets assigned to a mission that ends up being a lot more than she ever bargained for. Just like the Study trilogy, the plot of this book is really fast. There are a lot of different elements and things going on and it’s full of non-stop action and twists and turns. We get to travel to a few of the different clans around Sitia, especially one we haven’t learned about before and it’s really interesting how deep and developed the world is. It’s really awesome to learn how each clans uses magic and what their culture is like. One of my favorite parts was learning about the Stormdancers and how they use their powers. There are also some insights into a few different family and how their dynamics works and how that affects the different characters. One of the big themes in this book is how magic corrupts people and how it can turn them against their friends and family. It’s such a complex topic and I really enjoyed being able to explore it here. I felt like the ending was too rushed. Our characters got out of a pickle but nothing was really resolved except for the romance.<br /><br />The worst thing about this book is Opal and the reason is because she’s not Yelena. It’s completely unfair and biased but it’s how I feel. I didn’t enjoy this book as much because instead of a kick ass female lead, I got a teenage girl who is still dealing with a lot of pain and insecurities. It’s totally valid and these kinds of characters are also important to have in books because you never know who may be able to relate to them, I just wanted something different. Her narrative was really whiny and indecisive and sometimes even boring. I just wanted her to pick something and then stick to her guns. To feel her power and acknowledge it for how awesome it is and just use it to help her country. But it just took too long. It finally happened but almost at 90% and after a lottttt of complaining and almost giving up like 20 times, so by then it was too late.<br /><br />Another thing that really bothered me was the romance. In the first few chapters, I was sure that it was going to be a slow burn romance but then it ended up being this weird love triangle that was but wasn’t really. Opal made the choice to settle for a guy that was there but spent most of the time thinking about the tortured bad boy whom she had a connection with right at the beginning. It felt like a teen drama and then there was a really weird scene and poor girl ended up in an awful situation and it was just not the best.<br /><br />I enjoyed some of the new characters introduced and was extremely happy and excited to see some old ones again. The two male main characters were both kind of okay. I have a liking for one more than the other but that one didn’t see a lot of spotlight so we didn’t see a lot of development to his character. The other was kind of meh until the end where it seems he’s not as nice as he seems but we don’t know because that wasn’t actually resolved in this first book. Yelena and Leif came back and it was spectacular! I didn’t realize how much I didn’t like Opal until I had both her and Yelena in a scene and I just wanted to see what Yelena was thinking. Then we got the chance to see more into one of the Master Magician’s, Zitora, and she was just freaking awesome! I can’t wait to see more of her.<br /><br />Overall, I liked the book because of the plot and writing but the characters let me down a lot. I am hopeful that there’ll be more character development in the next book. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('MnGqMkys/YfigYjFn2JqGyXL6TR7sVh1sWDabCbjv46HySkFGRNK9CsrUQMF4BdYeCjBsctTyrKwzzhUJ0nxFA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/445303.Maria_V_Snyder"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1530814053p3/445303.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer5681322595448326770">When Maria V. Snyder was younger, she aspired to be a storm chaser in the American Midwest so she attended Pennsylvania State University and earned a Bachelor of Science degree in Meteorology. Much to her chagrin, forecasting the weather wasn’t in her skill set so she spent a number of years as an environmental meteorologist, which is not exciting...at all. Bored at work and needing a creative out</span>
  <span id="freeText5681322595448326770" style="display:none">When Maria V. Snyder was younger, she aspired to be a storm chaser in the American Midwest so she attended Pennsylvania State University and earned a Bachelor of Science degree in Meteorology. Much to her chagrin, forecasting the weather wasn’t in her skill set so she spent a number of years as an environmental meteorologist, which is not exciting...at all. Bored at work and needing a creative outlet, she started writing fantasy and science fiction stories. Over twenty novels and numerous short stories later, Maria’s learned a thing or three about writing. She’s been on the New York Times bestseller list, won a dozen awards, and has earned her Masters of Arts degree in Writing from Seton Hill University, where she is now a faculty member. Her favorite color is red. She loves dogs, but is allergic, instead she has a big black tom cat named…Kitty (apparently naming cats isn’t in her skill set either). Maria also has a husband and two children who are an inspiration for her writing when they aren't being a distraction. Note: She mentions her cat before her family. <br /><br />When she's not writing she's either playing volleyball, traveling, or taking pictures. Being a writer, though is a ton of fun. Where else can you take fencing lessons, learn how to ride a horse, study marital arts, learn how to pick a lock, take glass blowing classes and attend Astronomy Camp and call it research? Maria will be the first one to tell you it's not working as a meteorologist.<br /><br />Readers are welcome to check out her website for book excerpts, free short stories, maps, blog, and her schedule at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.MariaVSnyder.com">http://www.MariaVSnyder.com</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5681322595448326770" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
